The described changes\\n25: // are not applied directly, but contain an approximation of the final\\n26: // result that will be completed during apply by resolving any values that\\n27: // cannot be predicted.\\n28: //\\n29: // A plan must always be accompanied by the configuration it was built from,\\n30: // since the plan does not itself include all of the information required to\\n31: // make the changes indicated.\\n32: type Plan struct {\\n33: \\t// Mode is the mode under which this plan was created.\\n34: \\t//\\n35: \\t// This is only recorded to allow for UI differences when presenting plans\\n36: \\t// to the end-user, and so it must not be used to influence apply-time\\n37: \\t// behavior. The actions during apply must be described entirely by\\n38: \\t// the Changes field, regardless of how the plan was created.\\n39: \\t//\\n40: \\t// FIXME: destroy operations still rely on DestroyMode being set, because\\n41: \\t// there is no other source of this information in the plan. VariableValues can potentially contain\\n53: \\t// unknown values for a speculative plan, but the variable values must\\n54: \\t// all be known for a plan that will subsequently be applied.\\n55: \\t//\\n56: \\t// ApplyTimeVariables retains the names of any ephemeral variables that were\\n57: \\t// set (non-null) during the planning phase and must therefore be\\n58: \\t// re-supplied by the caller (potentially with different values) during\\n59: \\t// the apply phase. Ephemeral input variables are intended for populating\\n60: \\t// arguments for other ephemeral objects in the configuration, such as\\n61: \\t// provider configurations. The described changes\\n25: // are not applied directly, but contain an approximation of the final\\n26: // result that will be completed during apply by resolving any values that\\n27: // cannot be predicted.\\n28: //\\n29: // A plan must always be accompanied by the configuration it was built from,\\n30: // since the plan does not itself include all of the information required to\\n31: // make the changes indicated.\\n32: type Plan struct {\\n33: \\t// Mode is the mode under which this plan was created.\\n34: \\t//\\n35: \\t// This is only recorded to allow for UI differences when presenting plans\\n36: \\t// to the end-user, and so it must not be used to influence apply-time\\n37: \\t// behavior. The actions during apply must be described entirely by\\n38: \\t// the Changes field, regardless of how the plan was created.\\n39: \\t//\\n40: \\t// FIXME: destroy operations still rely on DestroyMode being set, because\\n41: \\t// there is no other source of this information in the plan. New behavior\\n42: \\t// should not be added based on this flag, and changing the flag should be\\n43: \\t// checked carefully against existing destroy behaviors.\\n44: \\tUIMode Mode\\n45: \\n46: \\t// VariableValues, VariableMarks, and ApplyTimeVariables together describe\\n47: \\t// how Terraform should decide the input variable values for the apply\\n48: \\t// phase if this plan is to be applied.\\n49: \\t//\\n50: \\t// VariableValues and VariableMarks describe persisted (non-ephemeral)\\n51: \\t// values that were set as part of the planning options and are to be\\n52: \\t// re-used during the apply phase. VariableValues can potentially contain\\n53: \\t// unknown values for a speculative plan, but the variable values must\\n54: \\t// all be known for a plan that will subsequently be applied.\\n55: \\t//\\n56: \\t// ApplyTimeVariables retains the names of any ephemeral variables that were\\n57: \\t// set (non-null) during the planning phase and must therefore be\\n58: \\t// re-supplied by the caller (potentially with different values) during\\n59: \\t// the apply phase. Ephemeral input variables are intended for populating\\n60: \\t// arguments for other ephemeral objects in the configuration, such as\\n61: \\t// provider configurations. Although the values for these variables can\\n62: \\t// change between plan and apply, their \\\"nullness\\\" may not.\\n63: \\tVariableValues     map[string]DynamicValue\\n64: \\tVariableMarks      map[string][]cty.PathValueMarks\\n65: \\tApplyTimeVariables collections.Set[string]\\n66: \\n67: \\tChanges           *ChangesSrc\\n68: \\tDriftedResources  []*ResourceInstanceChangeSrc\\n69: \\tDeferredResources []*DeferredResourceInstanceChangeSrc\\n70: \\tTargetAddrs       []addrs.Targetable\\n71: \\tForceReplaceAddrs []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\\n72: \\tBackend           Backend\\n73: \\n74: \\t// Complete is true if Terraform considers this to be a \\\"complete\\\" plan,\\n75: \\t// which is to say that it includes a planned action (even if no-op)\\n76: \\t// for every resource instance object that was mentioned across both\\n77: \\t// the desired state and prior state.\\n78: \\t//\\n79: \\t// If Complete is false then the plan might still be applyable (check\\n80: \\t// [Plan.Applyable]) but after applying it the operator should be reminded\\n81: \\t// to plan and apply again to hopefully make more progress towards\\n82: \\t// convergence.\\n83: \\t//\\n84: \\t// For an incomplete plan, other fields of this type may give more context\\n85: \\t// about why the plan is incomplete, which a UI layer could present to\\n86: \\t// the user as part of a warning that the plan is incomplete.\\n87: \\tComplete bool\\n88: \\n89: \\t// Applyable is true if both Terraform was able to create a plan\\n90: \\t// successfully and if the plan calls for making some sort of meaningful\\n91: \\t// change.\\n92: \\t//\\n93: \\t// If [Plan.Errored] is also set then that means the plan is non-applyable\\n94: \\t// due to an error. If not then the plan was created successfully but found\\n95: \\t// no material differences between desired and prior state, and so\\n96: \\t// applying this plan would achieve nothing.\\n97: \\tApplyable bool\\n98: \\n99: \\t// Errored is true if the Changes information is incomplete because\\n100: \\t// the planning operation failed. An errored plan cannot be applied,\\n101: \\t// but can be cautiously inspected for debugging purposes.\\n102: \\tErrored bool\\n103: \\n104: \\t// Checks captures a snapshot of the (probably-incomplete) check results\\n105: \\t// at the end of the planning process.\\n106: \\t//\\n107: \\t// If this plan is applyable (that is, if the planning process completed\\n108: \\t// without errors) then the set of checks here should be complete even\\n109: \\t// though some of them will likely have StatusUnknown where the check\\n110: \\t// condition depends on values we won't know until the apply step.\\n111: \\tChecks *states.CheckResults\\n112: \\n113: \\t// RelevantAttributes is a set of resource instance addresses and\\n114: \\t// attributes that are either directly affected by proposed changes or may\\n115: \\t// have indirectly contributed to them via references in expressions.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// This is the result of a heuristic and is intended only as a hint to\\n118: \\t// the UI layer in case it wants to emphasize or de-emphasize certain\\n119: \\t// resources. Don't use this to drive any non-cosmetic behavior, especially\\n120: \\t// including anything that would be subject to compatibility constraints.\\n121: \\tRelevantAttributes []globalref.ResourceAttr\\n122: \\n123: \\t// PrevRunState and PriorState both describe the situation that the plan\\n124: \\t// was derived from:\\n125: \\t//\\n126: \\t// PrevRunState is a representation of the outcome of the previous\\n127: \\t// Terraform operation, without any updates from the remote system but\\n128: \\t// potentially including some changes that resulted from state upgrade\\n129: \\t// actions.\\n130: \\t//\\n131: \\t// PriorState is a representation of the current state of remote objects,\\n132: \\t// which will differ from PrevRunState if the \\\"refresh\\\" step returned\\n133: \\t// different data, which might reflect drift.\\n134: \\t//\\n135: \\t// PriorState is the main snapshot we use for actions during apply.\\n136: \\t// PrevRunState is only here so that we can diff PriorState against it in\\n137: \\t// order to report to the user any out-of-band changes we've detected.\\n138: \\tPrevRunState *states.State\\n139: \\tPriorState   *states.State\\n140: \\n141: \\t// ExternalReferences are references that are being made to resources within\\n142: \\t// the plan from external sources.\\n143: \\t//\\n144: \\t// This is never recorded outside of Terraform. It is not written into the\\n145: \\t// binary plan file, and it is not written into the JSON structured outputs.\\n146: \\t// The testing framework never writes the plans out but holds everything in\\n147: \\t// memory as it executes, so there is no need to add any kind of\\n148: \\t// serialization for this field. This does mean that you shouldn't rely on\\n149: \\t// this field existing unless you have just generated the plan.\\n150: \\tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\\n151: \\n152: \\t// Overrides contains the set of overrides that were applied while making\\n153: \\t// this plan. We need to provide the same set of overrides when applying\\n154: \\t// the plan so we preserve them here. As with  ExternalReferences, this is\\n155: \\t// only used by the testing framework and so isn't written into any external\\n156: \\t// representation of the plan.\\n157: \\tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\\n158: \\n159: \\t// Timestamp is the record of truth for when the plan happened.\\n160: \\tTimestamp time.Time\\n161: \\n162: \\t// ProviderFunctionResults stores hashed results from all provider\\n163: \\t// function calls, so that calls during apply can be checked for\\n164: \\t// consistency.\\n165: \\tProviderFunctionResults []providers.FunctionHash\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: // ProviderAddrs returns a list of all of the provider configuration addresses\\n169: // referenced throughout the receiving plan.\\n170: //\\n171: // The result is de-duplicated so that each distinct address appears only once.\\n172: func (p *Plan) ProviderAddrs() []addrs.AbsProviderConfig {\\n173: \\tif p == nil || p.Changes == nil {\\n174: \\t\\treturn nil\\n175: \\t}\\n176: \\n177: \\t\\tkeys = append(keys, k)\\n189: \\t}\\n190: \\tsort.Strings(keys)\\n191: \\n192: \\tret := make([]addrs.AbsProviderConfig, len(keys))\\n193: \\tfor i, key := range keys {\\n194: \\t\\tret[i] = m[key]\\n195: \\t}\\n196: \\n197: \\treturn ret\\n198: }\\n199: \\n200: // Backend represents the backend-related configuration and other data as it\\n201: // existed when a plan was created.\\n202: In that case, it's up to the codepath making that decision to\n261: \t// decide which value would provide the most relevant explanation to the\n262: \t// end-user and return that. New Action\n328: //\t--------+-------------+-----------\n329: //\tCreate    true          NoOp\n330: //\tDelete    false         NoOp\n331: //\tReplace   true          Delete\n332: //\tReplace   false rc\n405: }\n406: \n407: // ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason allows for some extra user-facing\n408: // reasoning for why a particular change action was chosen for a particular\n409: // resource instance.\n410: //\n411: // This only represents sufficient detail to give a suitable explanation to\n412: // an end-user, and mustn't be used for any real decision-making during the\n413: // apply step.\n414: type ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason rune\n415: \n416: //go:generate go run golang.org/x/tools/cmd/stringer -type=ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason changes.go\n417: \n418: const (\n419: \t// In most cases there's no special reason for choosing a particular\n420: \t// action, which is represented by ResourceInstanceChangeNoReason.\n421: \tResourceInstanceChangeNoReason ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = 0\n422: \n423: \t// ResourceInstanceReplaceBecauseTainted indicates that the resource\n424: \t// instance must be replaced because its existing current object \tResourceInstanceReplaceByTriggers ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = 'D'\n438: \n439: \t// ResourceInstanceReplaceBecauseCannotUpdate indicates that the resource\n440: \t// instance is planned to be replaced because the provider has indicated\n441: \t// that a requested change cannot be applied as an update.\n442: \t//\n443: \t// In this case, the RequiredReplace field will typically be It doesn't consider the\\n165: \\t// fact that multiple objects for the same resource instance might be\\n166: \\t// present in the same plan; use the ObjectAddr method instead if you\\n167: \\t// need a unique address for a particular change.\\n168: \\tAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\\n169: \\n170: \\t// DeposedKey is the identifier for a deposed object associated with the\\n171: \\t// given instance, or states.NotDeposed if this change applies to the\\n172: \\t// current object.\\n173: \\t//\\n174: \\t// A Replace change for a resource with create_before_destroy set will\\n175: \\t// create a new DeposedKey temporarily during replacement.
